10041-8{_}2176{_}Time has mellowed them into harmony with the major part of the house, and the kindly Virginia creeper has done its utmost to conceal the fact that they are constructed of plebeian bricks which were baked in this country; but Matocton was Matocton long before these wings were built, and a mere affair of yesterday, such as the Revolution, antedates them.
10041-8{_}2177{_}They were not standing when Tarleton paid his famous visit to Matocton.
10041-8{_}2178{_}In the main hall, you may still see the stairs up which he rode on horseback, and the slashes which his saber hacked upon the hand-rail.
10041-8{_}2179{_}To the front of the mansion lies a close-shaven lawn, dotted with sundry oaks and maples; and thence, the formal gardens descend in six broad terraces.
10041-8{_}2180{_}There is when summer reigns no lovelier spot than this bright medley of squares and stars and triangles and circles--all Euclid in flowerage--which glow with multitudinous colors where the sun strikes.
10041-8{_}2181{_}You will find no new flowers at Matocton, though.
10041-8{_}2182{_}Here are verbenas, poppies, lavender and marigolds, sweet-william, hollyhocks and columbine, phlox, and larkspur, and meadowsweet, and heart's-ease, just as they were when Thomasine Musgrave, Matocton's first châtelaine, was wont to tend them; and of all floral parvenus the gardens are innocent.
10041-8{_}2183{_}Box-hedges mark the walkways.
10041-8{_}2184{_}The seventh terrace was, until lately, uncultivated, the trees having been cleared away to afford pasturage.
10041-8{_}2185{_}It is now closely planted with beeches, none of great size, and extends to a tangled thicket of fieldpines and cedar and sassafras and blackberry bushes, which again masks a drop of some ten feet to the river.
10041-8{_}2186{_}The beach here is narrow; at high tide, it is rarely more than fifteen feet in breadth, and is in many places completely submerged.
10041-8{_}2187{_}Past this, the river lapses into the horizon line without a break, save on an extraordinarily clear day when Bigelow's Island may be seen as a dim smudge upon the west.
10041-8{_}2188{_}All these things, Rudolph Musgrave regarded with curiously deep interest for one who had seen them so many times before.
10041-8{_}2189{_}Then, with a shrug of the shoulders, he sauntered forward across the lawn.
10041-8{_}2190{_}He had planned several appropriate speeches, but, when it came to the point of giving them utterance, he merely held out his hand in an awkward fashion, and said:  "Anne!"
10041-8{_}2191{_}She looked up from her reading.
10041-8{_}2192{_}She did this with two red-brown eyes that had no apparent limits to their depth.
10041-8{_}2193{_}Her hand was soft; it seemed quite lost in the broad palm of a man's hand.
10041-8{_}2194{_}"Dear Rudolph," she said, as simply as though they had parted yesterday, "it's awfully good to see you again."
10041-8{_}2195{_}Colonel Musgrave cleared his throat, and sat down beside her.
10041-8{_}2196{_}A moment later Colonel Musgrave cleared his throat once more.
10041-8{_}2197{_}Then Mrs. Charteris laughed.
10041-8{_}2198{_}It was a pleasant laugh--a clear, rippling carol of clean mirth that sparkled in her eyes, and dimpled in her wholesome cheeks.
10041-8{_}2199{_}"So!
10041-8{_}2200{_}do you find it very, very awkward?"
10041-8{_}2201{_}"Awkward!"
10041-8{_}2202{_}he cried.
10041-8{_}2203{_}Their glances met in a flash of comprehension which seemed to purge the air.
10041-8{_}2204{_}Musgrave was not in the least self-conscious now.
10041-8{_}2205{_}He laughed, and lifted an admonitory forefinger.
10041-8{_}2206{_}"Oh, good Cynara," he said, "I am not what I was.
10041-8{_}2207{_}And so I cannot do it, my dear--I really cannot possibly live up to the requirements of being a Buried Past.
10041-8{_}2208{_}In a proper story-book or play, I would have to come back from New Zealand or the Transvaal, all covered with glory and epaulets, and have found you in the last throes of consumption: instead, you have fattened, Anne, which a Buried Past never does, and which shows a sad lack of appreciation for my feelings.
10041-8{_}2209{_}And I--ah, my dear, I must confess that my hair is growing gray, and that my life has not been entirely empty without you, and that I ate and enjoyed two mutton-chops at luncheon, though I knew I should see you to-day.
10041-8{_}2210{_}I am afraid we are neither of us up to heroics, Anne.
10041-8{_}2211{_}So let's be sensible and comfy, my dear."
10041-8{_}2212{_}"You brute!"
10041-8{_}2213{_}she cried--not looking irreparably angry, yet not without a real touch of vexation; "don't you know that every woman cherishes the picture of her former lovers sitting alone in the twilight, and growing lackadaisical over undying memories and faded letters?
10041-8{_}2214{_}And you--you approach me, after I don't dare to think how many years, as calmly as if I were an old schoolmate of your mother's, and attempt to talk to me about mutton-chops!
10041-8{_}2215{_}You ought to be ashamed of yourself, Rudolph Musgrave.
10041-8{_}2216{_}You might, at least, have started a little at seeing me, and have clasped your hand to your heart, and have said, 'You, you!'
10041-8{_}2217{_}or something of the sort.
10041-8{_}2218{_}I had every right to expect it."
10041-8{_}2219{_}Mrs. Charteris pouted, and then trifled for a moment with the pages of her book.
10041-8{_}2220{_}"And--and I want to tell you that I am sorry for the way I spoke to you--that night," she swiftly said.
10041-8{_}2221{_}Anne did not look at him.
10041-8{_}2222{_}"Women don't understand things that are perfectly simple to men, I suppose--I mean--that is, Jack said--"  "That you ought to apologize?
10041-8{_}2223{_}It was very like him"--and Colonel Musgrave smiled to think how like John Charteris it was.
10041-8{_}2224{_}"Jack is quite wonderful," he observed.
10041-8{_}2225{_}She looked up, saying impulsively, "Rudolph, you don't know how happy he makes me."
10041-8{_}2226{_}"Heartless woman, and would you tempt me to end the tragedy of my life with a Shakesperian fifth act of poisonings and assassination?
10041-8{_}2227{_}I spurn you, temptress.
10041-8{_}2228{_}For, after all, it was an unpleasantly long while ago we went mad for each other," Musgrave announced, and he smiled.
10041-8{_}2229{_}"I fancy that the boy and girl we knew of are as dead now as Nebuchadnezzar.
10041-8{_}2230{_}'Marian's married, and I sit here alive and merry at'--well, not at forty year, unluckily--"  "If you continue in that heartless strain, I shall go into the house," Mrs. Charteris protested.
10041-8{_}2231{_}Her indignation was exaggerated, but it was not altogether feigned; women cannot quite pardon a rejected suitor who marries and is content.
10041-8{_}2232{_}They wish him all imaginable happiness and prosperity, of course; and they are honestly interested in his welfare; but it seems unexpectedly callous in him.
10041-8{_}2233{_}And besides his wife is so perfectly commonplace.
10041-8{_}2234{_}Mrs. Charteris, therefore, added, with emphasis: "I am really disgracefully happy."
10041-8{_}2235{_}"Glad to hear it," said Musgrave, placidly.
10041-8{_}2236{_}"So am I."
10041-8{_}2237{_}"Oh, Rudolph, Rudolph, you are hopeless!"
10041-8{_}2238{_}she sighed.
10041-8{_}2239{_}"And you used to make such a nice lover!"
10041-8{_}2240{_}Mrs. Charteris looked out over the river, which was like melting gold, and for a moment was silent.
10041-8{_}2241{_}"I was frightfully in love with you, Rudolph," she said, as half in wonder.
10041-8{_}2242{_}"After--after that horrible time when my parents forced us to behave rationally, I wept--oh, I must have wept deluges!
10041-8{_}2243{_}I firmly intended to pine away to an early grave.
10041-8{_}2244{_}And that second time I liked you too, but then--there was Jack, you see."
10041-8{_}2245{_}"H'm!"
10041-8{_}2246{_}said Colonel Musgrave; "yes, I see."
10041-8{_}2247{_}"I want you to continue to be friends with Jack," she went on, and her face lighted up, and her voice grew tender.
10041-8{_}2248{_}"He has the artistic temperament, and naturally that makes him sensitive, and a trifle irritable at times.
10041-8{_}2249{_}It takes so little to upset him, you see, for he feels so acutely what he calls the discords of life.
10041-8{_}2250{_}I think most men are jealous of his talents; so they call him selfish and finicky and conceited.
10041-8{_}2251{_}He isn't really, you know.
10041-8{_}2252{_}Only, he can't help feeling a little superior to the majority of men, and his artistic temperament leads him to magnify the lesser mishaps of life--such as the steak being overdone, or missing a train.
10041-8{_}2253{_}Oh, really, a thing like that worries him as much as the loss of a fortune, or a death in the family, would upset anyone else.
10041-8{_}2254{_}Jack says there are no such things as trifles in a harmonious and well-proportioned life, and I suppose that's true to men of genius.
10041-8{_}2255{_}Of course, I am rather a Philistine, and I grate on him at times--that is, I used to, but he says I have improved wonderfully.
10041-8{_}2256{_}And so we are ridiculously happy, Jack and I."
10041-8{_}2257{_}Musgrave cast about vainly for an appropriate speech.
10041-8{_}2258{_}Then he compromised with his conscience, and said: "Your husband is a very clever man."
10041-8{_}2259{_}"Isn't he?"
10041-8{_}2260{_}She had flushed for pleasure at hearing him praised.
10041-8{_}2261{_}Oh, yes, Anne loved Jack Charteris!
10041-8{_}2262{_}There was no questioning that; it was written in her face, was vibrant in her voice as she spoke of him.
10041-8{_}2263{_}"Now, really, Rudolph, aren't his books wonderful?
10041-8{_}2264{_}I don't appreciate them, of course, for I'm not clever, but I know you do.
10041-8{_}2265{_}I don't see why men think him selfish.
10041-8{_}2266{_}I know better.
10041-8{_}2267{_}You have to live with Jack to really appreciate him.
10041-8{_}2268{_}And every day I discover some new side of his character that makes him dearer to me.
10041-8{_}2269{_}He's so clever--and so noble.
10041-8{_}2270{_}Why, I remember--Well, before Jack made his first hit with _Astaroth's Lackey_, he lived with his sister.
10041-8{_}2271{_}They hadn't any money, and, of course, Jack couldn't be expected to take a clerkship or anything like that, because business details make his head ache, poor boy.
10041-8{_}2272{_}So, his sister taught school, and he lived with her.
10041-8{_}2273{_}They were very happy--his sister simply adores him, and I am positively jealous of her sometimes--but, unfortunately, the bank in which she kept her money failed one day.
10041-8{_}2274{_}I remember it was just before he asked me to marry him, and told me, in his dear, laughing manner, that he hadn't a penny in the world, and that we would have to live on bread and cheese and kisses.
10041-8{_}2275{_}Of course, I had a plenty for us both, though, so we weren't really in danger of being reduced to that.
10041-8{_}2276{_}Well, I wanted to make his sister an allowance.
10041-8{_}2277{_}But Jack pointed out, with considerable reason, that one person could live very comfortably on an income that had formerly supported two.
10041-8{_}2278{_}He said it wasn't right I should be burdened with the support of his family.
10041-8{_}2279{_}Jack was so sensitive, you see, lest people might think he was making a mercenary marriage, and that his sister was profiting by it.
10041-8{_}2280{_}Now, I call that one of the noblest things I ever heard of, for he is devotedly attached to his sister, and, naturally, it is a great grief to him to see her compelled to work for a living.
10041-8{_}2281{_}His last book was dedicated to her, and the dedication is one of the most tender and pathetic things I ever read."
10041-8{_}2282{_}Musgrave was hardly conscious of what she was saying.
10041-8{_}2283{_}She was not particularly intelligent, this handsome, cheery woman, but her voice, and the richness and sweetness of it, and the vitality of her laugh, contented his soul.
10041-8{_}2284{_}Anne was different; the knowledge came again to him quite simply that Anne was different, and in the nature of things must always be a little different from all other people--even Patricia Musgrave.
10041-8{_}2285{_}He had no desire to tell Anne Charteris of this, no idea that it would affect in any way the tenor of his life.
10041-8{_}2286{_}He merely accepted the fact that she was, after all, Anne Willoughby, and that her dear presence seemed, somehow, to strengthen and cheer and comfort and content beyond the reach of expression.
10041-8{_}2287{_}Yet Musgrave recognized her lack of cleverness, and liked and admired her none the less.
10041-8{_}2288{_}A vision of Patricia arose--a vision of a dainty, shallow, Dresden-china face with a surprising quantity of vivid hair about it.
10041-8{_}2289{_}Patricia was beautiful; and Patricia was clever, in her pinchbeck way.
10041-8{_}2290{_}But Rudolph Musgrave doubted very much if her mocking eyes now ever softened into that brooding, sacred tenderness he had seen in Anne's eyes; and he likewise questioned if a hurried, happy thrill ran through Patricia's voice when Patricia spoke of her husband.
10041-8{_}2291{_}"You have unquestionably married an unusual man," Musgrave said.
10041-8{_}2292{_}"I--by Jove, you know, I fancy my wife finds him almost as attractive as you do."
10041-8{_}2293{_}"Ah, Rudolph, I can't fancy anyone whom--whom you loved caring for anyone else.
10041-8{_}2294{_}Don't I remember, sir, how irresistible you can be when you choose?"
10041-8{_}2295{_}Anne laughed, and raised plump hands to heaven.
10041-8{_}2296{_}"Really, though, women pursue him to a perfectly indecent extent.
10041-8{_}2297{_}I have to watch over him carefully; not that I distrust him, of course, for--dear Jack!--he is so devoted to me, and cares so little for other women, that Joseph would seem in comparison only a depraved _roué_.
10041-8{_}2298{_}But the _women_--why, Rudolph, there was an Italian countess at Rome--the impudent minx!--who actually made me believe--However, Jack explained all that, after I had made both a spectacle and a nuisance of myself, and he had behaved so nobly in the entire affair that for days afterwards I was positively limp with repentance.
10041-8{_}2299{_}Then in Paris that flighty Mrs. Hardress--but he explained that, too.
10041-8{_}2300{_}Some women are shameless, Rudolph," Mrs. Charteris concluded, and sighed her pity for them.
10041-8{_}2301{_}"Utterly so," Musgrave assented, gravely.
10041-8{_}2302{_}He was feeling a thought uncomfortable.
10041-8{_}2303{_}To him the place had grown portentous.
10041-8{_}2304{_}The sun was low, and the long shadows of the trees were black on the dim lawn.
10041-8{_}2305{_}People were assembling for supper, and passing to and fro under low-hanging branches; and the gaily-colored gowns of the women glimmered through a faint blue haze like that with which Boucher and Watteau and Fragonard loved to veil, and thereby to make wistful, somehow, the antics of those fine parroquet-like manikins who figure in their _fêtes galantes._  Inside the house, someone was playing an unpleasant sort of air on the piano--an air which was quite needlessly creepy and haunting and insistent.
10041-8{_}2306{_}It all seemed like a grim bit out of a play.
10041-8{_}2307{_}The tenderness and pride that shone in Anne's eyes as she boasted of her happiness troubled Rudolph Musgrave.
10041-8{_}2308{_}He had a perfectly unreasonable desire to carry her away, by force, if necessary, and to protect her from clever people, and to buy things for her.
10041-8{_}2309{_}"So, I am an old, old married woman now, and--and I think in some ways I suit Jack better than a more brilliant person might.
10041-8{_}2310{_}I am glad your wife has taken a fancy to him.
10041-8{_}2311{_}And I want you to profit by her example.
10041-8{_}2312{_}Jack says she is one of the most attractive women he ever met.
10041-8{_}2313{_}He asked me to-day why I didn't do my hair like hers.
10041-8{_}2314{_}She must make you very happy, Rudolph?"
10041-8{_}2315{_}"My wife," Colonel Musgrave said, "is in my partial opinion, a very clever and very beautiful woman."
10041-8{_}2316{_}"Yes; cleverness and beauty are sufficient to make any man happy, I suppose," Anne hazarded.
10041-8{_}2317{_}"Jack says, though--_Are_ cleverness and beauty the main things in life, Rudolph?"
10041-8{_}2318{_}"Undoubtedly," he protested.
10041-8{_}2319{_}"Now, that," she said, judicially, "shows the difference in men.
10041-8{_}2320{_}Jack says a man loves a woman, not for her beauty or any other quality she possesses, but just because she is the woman he loves and can't help loving."
10041-8{_}2321{_}"Ah!
10041-8{_}2322{_}I dare say that is the usual reason.
10041-8{_}2323{_}Yes," said Colonel Musgrave,--"because she is the woman he loves and cannot help loving!"
10041-8{_}2324{_}Anne clapped her hands.
10041-8{_}2325{_}"Ah, so I have penetrated your indifference at last, sir!"
10041-8{_}2326{_}Impulsively, she laid her hand upon his arm, and spoke with earnestness.
10041-8{_}2327{_}"Dear Rudolph, I am so glad you've found the woman you can really love.
10041-8{_}2328{_}Jack says there is only one possible woman in the world for each man, and that only in a month of Sundays does he find her."
10041-8{_}2329{_}"Yes."
10041-8{_}2330{_}said Musgrave.
10041-8{_}2331{_}He had risen, and was looking down in friendly fashion into her honest, lovely eyes.
10041-8{_}2332{_}"Yes, there is only one possible woman.
10041-8{_}2333{_}And--yes, I think I found her, Anne, some years ago."
10041-8{_}2334{_}III   Thus it befell that all passed smoothly with Rudolph Musgrave and Anne Charteris, with whom he was not in the least in love any longer (he reflected), although in the nature of things she must always seem to him a little different from all other people.
10041-8{_}2335{_}And it befell, too, that the following noon--this day being a Sunday, warm, clear, and somnolent--Anne Charteris and Rudolph Musgrave sat upon the lawn before Matocton, and little Roger Musgrave was with them.
10041-8{_}2336{_}In fact, these two had been high-handedly press-ganged by this small despot to serve against an enemy then harassing his majesty's equanimity and by him, revilingly, designated as Nothing-to-do.
10041-8{_}2337{_}And so Anne made for Roger--as she had learned to do for her dead son--in addition to a respectable navy of paper boats, a vast number of "boxes" and "Nantucket sinks" and "picture frames" and "footballs."
10041-8{_}2338{_}She had used up the greater part of a magazine before the imp grew tired of her novel accomplishments.
10041-8{_}2339{_}For as he invidiously observed, "I can make them for myself now, most as good as you, only I always tear the bottom of the boat when you pull it out, and my sinks are kind of wobbly.
10041-8{_}2340{_}And besides, I've made up a story just like your husband gets money for doing.
10041-8{_}2341{_}And if I had a quarter I would buy that green and yellow snake in the toy-store window and wiggle it at people and scare them into fits."
10041-8{_}2342{_}"Sonnikins," said Colonel Musgrave, "suppose you tell us the story, and then we will see if it is really worth a quarter, and try to save you from this unblushing mendicancy."
10041-8{_}2343{_}"Well, God bless Father and Mother and little cousins--Oh, no, that's what I say at night."
10041-8{_}2344{_}Roger's voice now altered, assuming shrill singsong cadences.
10041-8{_}2345{_}His pensive gravity would have appeared excessive if manifested by the Great Sphinx.
10041-8{_}2346{_}"What I meant to say was that once upon a time when the Battle of Gettysburg was going on and houses were being robbed and burned, and my dear grandfather was being shot through the heart, a certain house, where the richest man in town lived, was having feast and merriment, never dreaming of any harm, or thinking of their little child Rachel, who was on the front porch watching the battle and screaming with joy at every man that fell dead.
10041-8{_}2347{_}One dark-faced man was struck with a bullet and was hurt.
10041-8{_}2348{_}He saw the child laughing at him and his heart was full of revenge.
10041-8{_}2349{_}So that night, when all had gone to bed, the old dark-faced man went softly in the house and got the little girl and set the house on fire.
10041-8{_}2350{_}And he carried her out in the mountains, and is that worth a quarter?"
10041-8{_}2351{_}"Good heavens, no!"
10041-8{_}2352{_}said Anne.
10041-8{_}2353{_}"How dare you leave us in such harrowing suspense?"
10041-8{_}2354{_}"Well, a whole lot more happened, because all the while Rachel was asleep.
10041-8{_}2355{_}When she woke up, she did not know where under the sun she was.
10041-8{_}2356{_}So she walked along for about an hour and came to a little village, and after a few minutes she came to a large rock, and guess who she met?
10041-8{_}2357{_}She met her father, and when he saw her he hugged her so hard that when he got through she did not have any breath left in her.
10041-8{_}2358{_}And they walked along, and after a while they came to the wood, and it was now about six o'clock, and it was very dark, and just then nine robbers jumped out from behind the trees, and they took a pistol and shot Rachel's father, and the child fainted.
10041-8{_}2359{_}Her papa was dead, so she dug a hole and buried him, and went right back home.
10041-8{_}2360{_}And of course that was all, and if I had that snake, I wouldn't try to scare you with it, father, anyhow."
10041-8{_}2361{_}So Colonel Musgrave gave his son a well-earned coin, as the colonel considered, and it having been decreed, "Now, father, _you_ tell a story," obediently read aloud from a fat red-covered book.
10041-8{_}2362{_}The tale was of the colonel's selecting, and it dealt with a shepherdess and a chimney-sweep.
10041-8{_}2363{_}"And so," the colonel perorated, "the little china people remained together, and were thankful for the rivet in grandfather's neck, and continued to love each other until they were broken to pieces--And the tale is a parable, my son.
10041-8{_}2364{_}You will find that out some day.
10041-8{_}2365{_}I wish you didn't have to."
10041-8{_}2366{_}"But is that all, father?"
10041-8{_}2367{_}"You will find it rather more than enough, sonnikins, when you begin to interpret.
10041-8{_}2368{_}Yes, that is all.
10041-8{_}2369{_}Only you are to remember always that they climbed to the very top of the chimney, where they could see the stars, before they decided to go back and live upon the parlor table under the brand-new looking-glass.
10041-8{_}2370{_}For the stars are disconcertingly unconcerned when you have climbed to them, and so altogether unimpressed by your achievement that it is the nature of all china people to slink home again, precisely as your Rachel did--and as Mrs. Charteris will assure you."
10041-8{_}2371{_}"I?"
10041-8{_}2372{_}said Anne.
10041-8{_}2373{_}"Now, honestly, Rudolph, I was thinking you ought not to let him sit upon the grass, because he really has a cold.
10041-8{_}2374{_}And if I were you, I would give him a good dose of castor-oil to-night.
10041-8{_}2375{_}Some people give it in lemon-juice, I know, but I found with my boy that peppermint is rather less disagreeable.
10041-8{_}2376{_}And you could easily send somebody over to the store at the station----"  Anne broke off short.
10041-8{_}2377{_}"Was I being inadequate again?
10041-8{_}2378{_}I am sorry, but with children you never know what a cold may lead to, and I really do not believe it good for him to sit in this damp grass."
10041-8{_}2379{_}"Sonnikins," said Rudolph Musgrave, "you had better climb up into my lap, before you and I are Podsnapped from the universe by the only embodiment of common-sense just now within our reach."
10041-8{_}2380{_}He patted the boy's head and latterly resumed: "I am afraid of you, Anne.
10041-8{_}2381{_}Whenever I am imagining vain things or stitching romantic possibilities, like embroideries, about the fabric of my past, I always find the real you in my path, as undeniable as a gas-bill.
10041-8{_}2382{_}I don't believe you ever dare to think, because there is no telling what it might lead to.
10041-8{_}2383{_}You are simply unassailably armored by the courage of other people's convictions."
10041-8{_}2384{_}Her candid eyes met his over the boy's bright head.
10041-8{_}2385{_}"And what in the world are you talking about?"
10041-8{_}2386{_}"I am lamenting.
10041-8{_}2387{_}I am rending the air and beating my breast on account of your obstinate preference for being always in the right.
10041-8{_}2388{_}I do wish you would endeavor to impersonate a human being a trifle more convincingly----"  But the great gong, booming out for luncheon, interrupted him at this point, and Colonel Musgrave was never permitted to finish his complaint against Anne's unimaginativeness.
10041-8{_}2389{_}IV   On that same Sunday morning, while Anne Charteris and Rudolph Musgrave contended with little Roger's boredom on the lawn before Matocton, Patricia and Charteris met by accident on the seventh terrace of the gardens.
10041-8{_}2390{_}Patricia had mentioned casually at the breakfast-table that she intended to spend the forenoon on this terrace unsabbatically making notes for a paper on "The Symbolism of Dante," which she was to read before the Lichfield Woman's Club in October; but Mr. Charteris had not overheard her.
10041-8{_}2391{_}He was seated on the front porch, working out a somewhat difficult point in his new book, when it had first occurred to him that this particular terrace would be an inspiring and appropriate place in which to think the matter over, undisturbed, he said.
10041-8{_}2392{_}And it was impossible he should have known that anyone was there, as the seventh terrace happens to be the only one that, being planted with beech-trees, is completely screened from observation.
10041-8{_}2393{_}From the house, you cannot see anything that happens there.
10041-8{_}2394{_}It was a curious accident, though.
10041-8{_}2395{_}It really seemed, now that Patricia had put an ending to their meetings in the maple-grove, Fate was conspiring to bring them together.
10041-8{_}2396{_}However, as Mr. Charteris pointed out, there could be no possible objection to this conspiracy, since they had decided that their friendship was to be of a purely platonic nature.
10041-8{_}2397{_}It was a severe trial to him, he confessed, to be forced to put aside certain dreams he had had of the future--mad dreams, perhaps, but such as had seemed very dear and very plausible to his impractical artistic temperament.
10041-8{_}2398{_}Still, it heartened him to hope that their friendship--since it was to be no more--might prove a survival, or rather a veritable renaissance, of the beautiful old Greek spirit in such matters.
10041-8{_}2399{_}And, though the blind chance that mismanaged the world had chained them to uncongenial, though certainly well-meaning, persons, this was no logical reason why he and Patricia should be deprived of the pleasures of intellectual intercourse.
10041-8{_}2400{_}Their souls were too closely akin.
10041-8{_}2401{_}For Mr. Charteris admitted that his soul was Grecian to the core, and out of place and puzzled and very lonely in a sordid, bustling world; and he assured Patricia--she did not object if he called her Patricia?--that her own soul possessed all the beauty and purity and calm of an Aphrodite sculptured by Phidias.
10041-8{_}2402{_}It was such a soul as Horace might have loved, as Theocritus might have hymned in glad Greek song.
10041-8{_}2403{_}Patricia flushed, and dissented somewhat.
10041-8{_}2404{_}"Frankly, _mon ami_," she said, "you are far too attractive for your company to be quite safe.
10041-8{_}2405{_}You are such an adept in the nameless little attentions that women love--so profuse with lesser sugar-plums of speech and action--that after two weeks one's husband is really necessary as an antidote.
10041-8{_}2406{_}Sugar-plums are good, but, like all palatable things, unwholesome.
10041-8{_}2407{_}So I shall prescribe Rudolph's company for myself, to ward off an attack of moral indigestion.
10041-8{_}2408{_}I am very glad he has come back--really glad," she added, conscientiously.
10041-8{_}2409{_}"Poor old Rudolph!
10041-8{_}2410{_}what between his interminable antiquities and those demented sections of the alphabet--What are those things, _mon ami_, that are always going up and down in Wall Street?"
10041-8{_}2411{_}"Elevators?"
10041-8{_}2412{_}Mr. Charteris suggested.
10041-8{_}2413{_}"Oh, you jay-bird!
10041-8{_}2414{_}I mean those N.P.
10041-8{_}2415{_}'s and N.Y.C.
10041-8{_}2416{_}'s and those other letters that are always having flurries and panics and passed dividends.
10041-8{_}2417{_}They keep him incredibly busy."
10041-8{_}2418{_}And she sighed, tolerantly.
10041-8{_}2419{_}Patricia had come within the last two weeks to believe that she was neglected, if not positively ill-treated, by her husband; and she had no earthly objection to Mr. Charteris thinking likewise.
10041-8{_}2420{_}Her face expressed patient resignation now, as they walked under the close-matted foliage of the beech-trees, which made a pleasant, sun-flecked gloom about them.
10041-8{_}2421{_}Patricia removed her hat--the morning really was rather close--and paused where a sunbeam fell upon her copper-colored hair, and glorified her wistful countenance.
10041-8{_}2422{_}She sighed once more, and added a finishing touch to the portrait of a _femme incomprise_.
10041-8{_}2423{_}"Pray, don't think, _mon ami_," she said very earnestly, "that I am blaming Rudolph!
10041-8{_}2424{_}I suppose no wife can ever hope to have any part in her husband's inner life."
10041-8{_}2425{_}"Not in her own husband's, of course," said Charteris, cryptically.
10041-8{_}2426{_}"No, for while a woman gives her heart all at once, men crumble theirs away, as one feeds bread to birds--a crumb to this woman, a crumb to that--and such a little crumb, sometimes!
10041-8{_}2427{_}And his wife gets what is left over."
10041-8{_}2428{_}"Pray, where did you read that?"
10041-8{_}2429{_}said Charteris.
10041-8{_}2430{_}"I didn't read it anywhere.
10041-8{_}2431{_}It was simply a thought that came to me," Patricia lied, gently.
10041-8{_}2432{_}"But don't let's try to be clever.
10041-8{_}2433{_}Cleverness is always a tax, but before luncheon it is an extortion.
10041-8{_}2434{_}Personally, it makes me feel as if I had attended a welsh-rabbit supper the night before.
10041-8{_}2435{_}Your wife must be very patient."
10041-8{_}2436{_}"My wife," cried Charteris, in turn resolved to screen an unappreciative mate, "is the most dear and most kind-hearted among the Philistines.
10041-8{_}2437{_}And yet, at times, I grant you--"  "Oh, but, of course!"
10041-8{_}2438{_}Patricia said impatiently.
10041-8{_}2439{_}"I don't for a moment question that your wife is an angel."
10041-8{_}2440{_}"And why?"
10041-8{_}2441{_}His eyebrows lifted, and he smiled.
10041-8{_}2442{_}"Why, wasn't it an angel," Patricia queried, all impishness now, "who kept the first man and woman out of paradise?"
10041-8{_}2443{_}"If--if I thought you meant that----!"
10041-8{_}2444{_}he cried; and then he shrugged his shoulders.
10041-8{_}2445{_}"My wife's virtues merit a better husband than Fate has accorded her.
10041-8{_}2446{_}Anne is the best woman I have ever known."
10041-8{_}2447{_}Patricia was not unnaturally irritated.
10041-8{_}2448{_}After all, one does not take the trouble to meet a man accidentally in a plantation of young beech-trees in order to hear him discourse of his wife's good qualities; and besides, Mr. Charteris was speaking in a disagreeably solemn manner, rather as if he fancied himself in a cathedral.
10041-8{_}2449{_}Therefore Patricia cast down her eyes again, and said:  "Men of genius are so rarely understood by their wives."
10041-8{_}2450{_}"We will waive the question of genius."
10041-8{_}2451{_}Mr. Charteris laughed heartily, but he had flushed with pleasure.
10041-8{_}2452{_}"I suppose," he continued, pacing up and down with cat-like fervor, "that matrimony is always more or less of a compromise--like two convicts chained together trying to catch each other's gait.
10041-8{_}2453{_}After a while, they succeed to a certain extent; the chain is still heavy, of course, but it does not gall them as poignantly as it used to do.
10041-8{_}2454{_}And I fear the artistic temperament is not suited to marriage; its capacity for suffering is too great."
10041-8{_}2455{_}Mr. Charteris caught his breath in shuddering fashion, and he paused before Patricia.
10041-8{_}2456{_}After a moment he grasped her by both wrists.
10041-8{_}2457{_}"We are chained fast enough, my lady," he cried, bitterly, "and our sentence is for life!
10041-8{_}2458{_}There are green fields yonder, but our allotted place is here in the prison-yard.
10041-8{_}2459{_}There is laughter yonder in the fields, and the scent of wild flowers floats in to us at times when we are weary, and the whispering trees sway their branches over the prison-wall, and their fruit is good to look on, and they hang within reach--ah, we might reach them very easily!
10041-8{_}2460{_}But this is forbidden fruit, my lady; and it is not included in our wholesome prison-fare.
10041-8{_}2461{_}And so don't think of it!
10041-8{_}2462{_}We have been happy, you and I, for a little.
10041-8{_}2463{_}We might--don't think of it!
10041-8{_}2464{_}Don't dare think of it!
10041-8{_}2465{_}Go back and help your husband drag his chain; it galls him as sorely as it does you.
10041-8{_}2466{_}It galls us all.
10041-8{_}2467{_}It is the heaviest chain was ever forged; but we do not dare shake it off!"
10041-8{_}2468{_}"I--oh, Jack, Jack, don't you dare to talk to me like that!
10041-8{_}2469{_}We must be brave.
10041-8{_}2470{_}We must be sensible."
10041-8{_}2471{_}Patricia, regardless of her skirts, sat down upon the ground, and produced a pocket-handkerchief.
10041-8{_}2472{_}"I--oh, what do you mean by making me so unhappy?"
10041-8{_}2473{_}she demanded, indignantly.
10041-8{_}2474{_}"Ah, Patricia," he murmured, as he knelt beside her, "how can you hope to have a man ever talk to you in a sane fashion?
10041-8{_}2475{_}You shouldn't have such eyes, Patricia!
10041-8{_}2476{_}They are purple and fathomless like the ocean, and when a man looks into them too long his sanity grows weak, and sinks and drowns in their cool depths, and the man must babble out his foolish heart to you.
10041-8{_}2477{_}Oh, but indeed, you shouldn't have such eyes, Patricia!
10041-8{_}2478{_}They are dangerous, and to ask anybody to believe in their splendor is an insult to his intelligence, and besides, they are much too bright to wear in the morning.
10041-8{_}2479{_}They are bad form, Patricia."
10041-8{_}2480{_}"We must be sensible," she babbled.
10041-8{_}2481{_}"Your wife is here; my husband is here.
10041-8{_}2482{_}And we--we aren't children or madmen, Jack dear.
10041-8{_}2483{_}So we really must be sensible, I suppose.
10041-8{_}2484{_}Oh, Jack," she cried, upon a sudden; "this isn't honorable!"
10041-8{_}2485{_}"Why, no!
10041-8{_}2486{_}Poor little Anne!"
10041-8{_}2487{_}Mr. Charteris's eyes grew tender for a moment, because his wife, in a fashion, was dear to him.
10041-8{_}2488{_}Then he laughed, very musically.
10041-8{_}2489{_}"And how can a man remember honor, Patricia, when the choice lies between honor and you?
10041-8{_}2490{_}You shouldn't have such hair, Patricia!
10041-8{_}2491{_}It is a net spun out of the raw stuff of fire and blood and of portentous sunsets; and its tendrils have curled around what little honor I ever boasted, and they hold it fast, Patricia.
10041-8{_}2492{_}It is dishonorable to love you, but I cannot think of that when I am with you and hear you speak.
10041-8{_}2493{_}And when I am not with you, just to remember that dear voice is enough to set my pulses beating faster.
10041-8{_}2494{_}Oh, Patricia, you shouldn't have such a voice!"
10041-8{_}2495{_}Charteris broke off in speech.
10041-8{_}2496{_}"'Scuse me for interruptin'," the old mulattress Virginia was saying, "but Mis' Pilkins sen' me say lunch raydy, Miss Patrisy."
10041-8{_}2497{_}Virginia seemed to notice nothing out-of-the-way.
10041-8{_}2498{_}Having delivered her message, she went away quietly, her pleasant yellow face as imperturbable as an idol's.
10041-8{_}2499{_}But Patricia shivered.
10041-8{_}2500{_}"She frightens me, _mon ami_.
10041-8{_}2501{_}Yes, that old woman always gives me gooseflesh, and I don't know why--because she is as deaf as a post--and I simply can't get rid of her.
10041-8{_}2502{_}She is a sort of symbol--she, and how many others, I wonder!...
10041-8{_}2503{_}Oh, well, let's hurry."
10041-8{_}2504{_}So Mr. Charteris was never permitted to finish his complaint against Patricia's voice.
10041-8{_}2505{_}It was absolutely imperative they should be on time for luncheon; for, as Patricia pointed out, the majority of people are censorious and lose no opportunity for saying nasty things.
10041-8{_}2506{_}They are even capable of sneering at a purely platonic friendship which is attempting to preserve the beautiful old Greek spirit.
10041-8{_}2507{_}*       *       *       *       *  She was chattering either of her plans for the autumn, or of Dante and the discovery of his missing cantos, or else of how abominably Bob Townsend had treated Rosalind Jemmett, and they had almost reached the upper terrace--little Roger, indeed, his red head blazing in the sunlight, was already sidling by shy instalments toward them--when Patricia moaned inconsequently and for no ascertainable cause fainted.
10041-8{_}2508{_}It was the first time for four years she had been guilty of such an indiscretion, she was shortly afterward explaining to various members of the Musgraves' house-party.
10041-8{_}2509{_}It was the heat, no doubt.
10041-8{_}2510{_}But since everybody insisted upon it, she would very willingly toast them in another bumper of aromatic spirits of ammonia.
10041-8{_}2511{_}"Just look at that, Rudolph!
10041-8{_}2512{_}you've spilt it all over your coat sleeve.
10041-8{_}2513{_}I do wish you would try to be a little less clumsy.
10041-8{_}2514{_}Oh, well, I'm spruce as a new penny now.
10041-8{_}2515{_}So let's all go to luncheon."
10041-8{_}2516{_}V   Patricia had not been in perfect health for a long while.
10041-8{_}2517{_}It seemed to her, in retrospect, that ever since the agonies of little Roger's birth she had been the victim of what she described as "a sort of all-overishness."
10041-8{_}2518{_}Then, too, as has been previously recorded, Patricia had been operated upon by surgeons, and more than once....  "Good Lord!"
10041-8{_}2519{_}as she herself declared, "it has reached the point that when I see a turkey coming to the dinner-table to be carved I can't help treating it as an ingénue."
10041-8{_}2520{_}Yet for the last four years she had never fainted, until this.
10041-8{_}2521{_}It disquieted her.
10041-8{_}2522{_}Then, too, awoke faint pricking memories of certain symptoms ... which she had not talked about ...  Now they alarmed her; and in consequence she took the next morning's train to Lichfield.
10041-8{_}2523{_}VI   Mrs. Ashmeade, who has been previously quoted, now comes into the story.
10041-8{_}2524{_}She is only an episode.
10041-8{_}2525{_}Still, her intervention led to peculiar results--results, curiously enough, in which she was not in the least concerned.
10041-8{_}2526{_}She simply comes into the story for a moment, and then goes out of it; but her part is an important one.
10041-8{_}2527{_}She is like the watchman who announces the coming of Agamemnon; Clytemnestra sharpens her ax at the news, and the fatal bath is prepared for the _anax andron_.
10041-8{_}2528{_}The tragedy moves on; the house of Atreus falls, and the wrath of implacable gods bellows across the heavens; meanwhile, the watchman has gone home to have tea with his family, and we hear no more of him.
10041-8{_}2529{_}There are any number of morals to this.
10041-8{_}2530{_}Mrs. Ashmeade comes into the story on the day Patricia went to Lichfield, and some weeks after John Charteris's arrival at Matocton.
10041-8{_}2531{_}Since then, affairs had progressed in a not unnatural sequence.
10041-8{_}2532{_}Mr. Charteris, as we have seen, attributed it to Fate; and, assuredly, there must be a special providence of some kind that presides over country houses--a freakish and whimsical providence, which hugely rejoices in confounding one's sense of time and direction.
10041-8{_}2533{_}Through its agency, people unaccountably lose their way in the simplest walks, and turn up late and embarrassed for luncheon.
10041-8{_}2534{_}At the end of the evening, it brings any number of couples blinking out of the dark, with no idea the clock was striking more than half-past nine.
10041-8{_}2535{_}And it delights in sending one into the garden--in search of roses or dahlias or upas-trees or something of the sort, of course--and thereby causing one to encounter the most unlikely people, and really, quite the last person one would have thought of meeting, as all frequenters of house-party junketings will assure you.
10041-8{_}2536{_}And thus is this special house-party providence responsible for a great number of marriages, and, it may be, for a large percentage of the divorce cases; for, if you desire very heartily to see anything of another member of a house-party, this lax-minded and easy-going providence will somehow always bring the event about in a specious manner, and without any apparent thought of the consequences.
10041-8{_}2537{_}And the Musgraves' house-party was no exception.
10041-8{_}2538{_}Mrs. Ashmeade, for reasons of her own, took daily note of this.
10041-8{_}2539{_}The others were largely engrossed by their own affairs; they did not seriously concern themselves about the doings of their fellow-guests.
10041-8{_}2540{_}And, besides, if John Charteris manifestly sought the company of Patricia Musgrave, her husband did not appear to be exorbitantly dissatisfied or angry or even lonely; and, be this as it might, the fact remained that Celia Reindan was at this time more than a little interested in Teddy Anstruther; and Felix Kennaston was undeniably very attentive to Kathleen Saumarez; and Tom Gelwix was quite certainly devoting the major part of his existence to sitting upon the beach with Rosalind Jemmett.
10041-8{_}2541{_}For, in Lichfield at all events, everyone's house has at least a pane or so of glass in it; and, if indiscriminate stone-throwing were ever to become the fashion, there is really no telling what damage might ensue.
10041-8{_}2542{_}And so had Mrs. Ashmeade been a younger woman--had time and an adoring husband not rendered her as immune to an insanity _à deux_ as any of us may hope to be upon this side of saintship or senility--why, Mrs. Ashmeade would most probably have remained passive, and Mrs. Ashmeade would never have come into this story at all.
10041-8{_}2543{_}As it was, she approached Rudolph Musgrave with a fixed purpose this morning as he smoked an after-breakfast cigarette on the front porch of Matocton.
10041-8{_}2544{_}And,  "Rudolph," said Mrs. Ashmeade, "are you blind?"
10041-8{_}2545{_}"You mean--?"
10041-8{_}2546{_}he asked, and he broke off, for he had really no conception of what she meant.
10041-8{_}2547{_}And Mrs. Ashmeade said, "I mean Patricia and Charteris.
10041-8{_}2548{_}Did you think I was by any chance referring to the man in the moon and the Queen of Sheba?"
10041-8{_}2549{_}If ever amazement showed in a man's eyes, it shone now in Rudolph Musgrave's.
10041-8{_}2550{_}After a little, the pupils widened in a sort of terror.
10041-8{_}2551{_}So this was what Clarice Pendomer had been hinting at.
10041-8{_}2552{_}"Nonsense!"
10041-8{_}2553{_}he cried.
10041-8{_}2554{_}"Why--why, it is utter, preposterous, Bedlamite nonsense!"
10041-8{_}2555{_}He caught his breath in wonder at the notion of such a jest, remembering a little packet of letters hidden in his desk.
10041-8{_}2556{_}"It--oh, no, Fate hasn't quite so fine a sense of humor as that.
10041-8{_}2557{_}The thing is incredible!"
10041-8{_}2558{_}Musgrave laughed, and flushed.
10041-8{_}2559{_}"I mean----"  "I don't think you need tell me what you mean," said Mrs. Ashmeade.
10041-8{_}2560{_}She sat down in a large rocking-chair, and fanned herself, for the day was warm.
10041-8{_}2561{_}"Of course, it is officious and presumptuous and disagreeable of me to meddle.
10041-8{_}2562{_}I don't mind your thinking that.
10041-8{_}2563{_}But Rudolph, don't make the mistake of thinking that Fate ever misses a chance of humiliating us by showing how poor are our imaginations.
10041-8{_}2564{_}The gipsy never does.
10041-8{_}2565{_}She is a posturing mountebank, who thrives by astounding humanity."
10041-8{_}2566{_}Mrs. Ashmeade paused, and her eyes were full of memories, and very wise.
10041-8{_}2567{_}"I am only a looker-on at the tragic farce that is being played here," she continued, after a little, "but lookers-on, you know, see most of the game.
10041-8{_}2568{_}They are not playing fairly with you, Rudolph.
10041-8{_}2569{_}When people set about an infringement of the Decalogue they owe it to their self-respect to treat with Heaven as a formidable antagonist.
10041-8{_}2570{_}To mark the cards is not enough.
10041-8{_}2571{_}They are not playing fairly, my dear, and you ought to know it."
10041-8{_}2572{_}He walked up and down the porch once or twice, with his hands behind him; then he stopped before Mrs. Ashmeade, and smiled down at her.
10041-8{_}2573{_}Without, many locusts shrilled monotonously.
10041-8{_}2574{_}"No, I do not think you are officious or meddling or anything of the sort, I think you are one of the best and kindest-hearted women in the world.
10041-8{_}2575{_}But--bless your motherly soul, Polly!
10041-8{_}2576{_}the thing is utterly preposterous.
10041-8{_}2577{_}Of course, Patricia is young, and likes attention, and it pleases her to have men admire her.
10041-8{_}2578{_}That, Polly, is perfectly natural.
10041-8{_}2579{_}Why, you wouldn't expect her to sit around under the trees, and read poetry with her own husband, would you?
10041-8{_}2580{_}We have been married far too long for that, Patricia and I.
10041-8{_}2581{_}She thinks me rather prosy and stupid at times, poor girl, because--well, because, in point of fact, I am.
10041-8{_}2582{_}But, at the bottom of her heart--Oh, it's preposterous!
10041-8{_}2583{_}We are the best friends in the world, I tell you!
10041-8{_}2584{_}It is simply that she and Jack have a great deal in common--"  "You don't understand John Charteris.
10041-8{_}2585{_}I do," said Mrs. Ashmeade, placidly.
10041-8{_}2586{_}"Charteris is simply a baby with a vocabulary.
10041-8{_}2587{_}His moral standpoint is entirely that of infancy.
10041-8{_}2588{_}It would be ludicrous to describe him as selfish, because he is selfishness incarnate.
10041-8{_}2589{_}I sometimes believe it is the only characteristic the man possesses.
10041-8{_}2590{_}He reaches out his hand and takes whatever he wants, just as a baby would, quite simply, and as a matter of course.
10041-8{_}2591{_}He wants your wife now, and he is reaching out his hand to take her.
10041-8{_}2592{_}He probably isn't conscious of doing anything especially wrong; he is always so plausible in whatever he does that he ends by deceiving himself, I suppose.
10041-8{_}2593{_}For he is always plausible.
10041-8{_}2594{_}It is worse than useless to argue any matter with him, because he invariably ends by making you feel as if you had been caught stealing a hat.
10041-8{_}2595{_}The only argument that would get the better of John Charteris is knocking him down, just as spanking is the only argument which ever gets the better of a baby.
10041-8{_}2596{_}Yes, he is very like a baby--thoroughly selfish and thoroughly dependent on other people; only, he is a clever baby who exaggerates his own helplessness in order to appeal to women.
10041-8{_}2597{_}He has a taste for women.
10041-8{_}2598{_}And women naturally like him, for he impresses them as an irresponsible child astray in an artful and designing world.
10041-8{_}2599{_}They want to protect him.
10041-8{_}2600{_}Even I do, at times.
10041-8{_}2601{_}It is really maternal, you know; we would infinitely prefer for him to be soft and little, so that we could pick him up, and cuddle him.
10041-8{_}2602{_}But as it is, he is dangerous.
10041-8{_}2603{_}He believes whatever he tells himself, you see."
10041-8{_}2604{_}Her voice died away, and Mrs. Ashmeade fanned herself in the fashion addicted by perturbed women who, nevertheless, mean to have their say out--slowly and impersonally, and quite as if she was fanning some one else through motives of charity.
10041-8{_}2605{_}"I don't question," Musgrave said, at length, "that Jack is the highly estimable character you describe.
10041-8{_}2606{_}But--oh, it is all nonsense, Polly!"
10041-8{_}2607{_}he cried, with petulance, and with a tinge--if but the merest nuance --of conviction lacking in his voice.
10041-8{_}2608{_}The fan continued its majestic sweep from the shade into the sunlight, and back again into the shadow.
10041-8{_}2609{_}Without, many locusts shrilled monotonously.
10041-8{_}2610{_}"Rudolph, I know what you meant by saying that Fate hadn't such a fine sense of humor."
10041-8{_}2611{_}"My dear madam, it was simply thrown out, in the heat of conversation--as an axiom----"  For a moment the fan paused; then went on as before.
10041-8{_}2612{_}It was never charged against Pauline Ashmeade, whatever her shortcomings, that she was given to unnecessary verbiage.
10041-8{_}2613{_}Colonel Musgrave was striding up and down, divided between a disposition to swear at the universe at large and a desire to laugh at it.
10041-8{_}2614{_}Somehow, it did not occur to him to doubt what she had told him.
10041-8{_}2615{_}He comprehended now that, chafing under his indebtedness in the affair of Mrs. Pendomer, Charteris would most naturally retaliate by making love to his benefactor's wife, because the colonel also knew John Charteris.
10041-8{_}2616{_}And for the rest, it was useless to struggle against a Fate that planned such preposterous and elaborate jokes; one might more rationally depend on Fate to work out some both ludicrous and horrible solution, he reflected, remembering a little packet of letters hidden in his desk.
10041-8{_}2617{_}Nevertheless, he paused after a while, and laughed, with a tolerable affectation of mirth.
10041-8{_}2618{_}"I say--I--and what in heaven's name, Polly, prompted you to bring me this choice specimen of a mare's-nest?"
10041-8{_}2619{_}"Because I am fond of you, I suppose.
10041-8{_}2620{_}Isn't one always privileged to be disagreeable to one's friends?
10041-8{_}2621{_}We have been friends a long while, you know."
10041-8{_}2622{_}Mrs. Ashmeade was looking out over the river now, but she seemed to see a great way, a very great way, beyond its glaring waters, and to be rather uncertain as to whether what she beheld there was of a humorous or pathetic nature.
10041-8{_}2623{_}"Rudolph, do you remember that evening--the first summer that I knew you--at Fortress Monroe, when we sat upon the pier so frightfully late, and the moon rose out of the bay, and made a great, solid-looking, silver path that led straight over the rim of the world, and you talked to me about--about what, now?"
10041-8{_}2624{_}"Oh, yes, yes!--I remember perfectly!
10041-8{_}2625{_}One of the most beautiful evenings I ever saw.
10041-8{_}2626{_}I remember it quite distinctly.
10041-8{_}2627{_}I talked--I--and what, in the Lord's name, did I talk about, Polly?"
10041-8{_}2628{_}"Ah, men forget!
10041-8{_}2629{_}A woman never forgets when she is really friends with a man.
10041-8{_}2630{_}I know now you were telling me about Anne Charteris, for you have been in love with her all your life, Rudolph, in your own particular half-hearted and dawdling fashion.
10041-8{_}2631{_}Perhaps that is why you have had so many affairs.
10041-8{_}2632{_}You plainly found the run of women so unimportant that it put every woman on her pride to prove she was different.
10041-8{_}2633{_}Yes, I remember.
10041-8{_}2634{_}But that night I thought you were trying to make love to me, and I was disappointed in you, and--yes, rather pleased.
10041-8{_}2635{_}Women are all vain and perfectly inconsistent.
10041-8{_}2636{_}But then, girl-children always take after their fathers."
10041-8{_}2637{_}Mrs. Ashmeade rose from her chair.
10041-8{_}2638{_}Her fan shut with a snap.
10041-8{_}2639{_}"You were a dear boy, Rudolph, when I first knew you--and what I liked was that you never made love to me.
10041-8{_}2640{_}Of all the boys I have known and helped to form, you were the only sensible one--the only one who never presumed.
10041-8{_}2641{_}That was rather clever of you, Rudolph.
10041-8{_}2642{_}It would have been ridiculous, for even arithmetically I am older than you.
10041-8{_}2643{_}"Wouldn't it have been ridiculous, Rudolph?"
10041-8{_}2644{_}she demanded, suddenly.
10041-8{_}2645{_}"Not in the least," Musgrave protested, in courteous wise.
10041-8{_}2646{_}"You--why, Polly, you were a wonderfully handsome woman.
10041-8{_}2647{_}Any boy----"  "Oh, yes!--I was.
10041-8{_}2648{_}I'm not now, am I, Rudolph?"
10041-8{_}2649{_}Mrs. Ashmeade threw back her head and laughed naturally.
10041-8{_}2650{_}"Ah, dear boy that was, it is unfair, isn't it, for an old woman to seize upon you in this fashion, and insist on your making love to her?
10041-8{_}2651{_}But I will let you off.
10041-8{_}2652{_}You don't have to do it."
10041-8{_}2653{_}She caught her skirts in her left hand, preparatory to going, and her right hand rested lightly on his arm.
10041-8{_}2654{_}She spoke in a rather peculiar voice.
10041-8{_}2655{_}"Yes," she said, "the boy was a very, very dear boy, and I want the man to be equally brave and--sensible."
10041-8{_}2656{_}Musgrave stared after her.
10041-8{_}2657{_}"I wonder--I wonder--?
10041-8{_}2658{_}Oh, no, that couldn't be," he said, and wearily.
10041-8{_}2659{_}"There must be some preposterous situations that don't come about."
10041-8{_}2660{_}*       *       *       *       *  And afterward he strolled across the lawn, where the locusts were shrilling, as if in a stubborn prediction of something which was inevitable, and he meditated upon a great number of things.
10041-8{_}2661{_}There were a host of fleecy little clouds in the sky.
10041-8{_}2662{_}He looked up at them, interrogatively.
10041-8{_}2663{_}And then he smiled and shook his head.
10041-8{_}2664{_}"Yet I don't know," said he; "for I am coming to the conclusion that the world is run on an extremely humorous basis."
10041-8{_}2665{_}And oddly enough, it was at the same moment that Patricia--in Lichfield--reached the same conclusion.
10041-8{_}2666{_}PART SEVEN - YOKED    "We are as time moulds us, lacking wherewithal   To shape out nobler fortunes or contend   Against all-patient Fates, who may not mend   The allotted pattern of things temporal   Or alter it a jot or e'er let fall   A single stitch thereof, until at last   The web and its drear weavers be overcast   And predetermined darkness swallow all.
10041-8{_}2667{_}"They have ordained for us a time to sing,   A time to love, a time wherein to tire   Of all spent songs and kisses; caroling   Such elegies as buried dreams require,   Love now departs, and leaves us shivering   Beside the embers of a burned-out fire."
10041-8{_}2668{_}PAUL VANDERHOFFEN.
10041-8{_}2669{_}_Egeria Answers._     I   The doctor's waiting-room smelt strongly of antiseptics.
10041-8{_}2670{_}That was Patricia's predominating thought as she wandered aimlessly about the apartment.
10041-8{_}2671{_}She fingered its dusty furniture.
10041-8{_}2672{_}She remembered afterward the steel-engraving of Jefferson Davis and his Cabinet, with General Lee explaining some evidently important matter to those attentive and unhumanly stiff politicians; and she remembered, too, how in depicting one statesman, who unavoidably sat with his back to the spectator, the artist had exceeded anatomical possibilities in order to obtain a recognizable full-faced portrait.
10041-8{_}2673{_}Yet at the time this picture had not roused her conscious attention.
10041-8{_}2674{_}She went presently to the long table austerely decorated with two rows of magazines, each partly covered by its neighbor, just as shingles are placed.
10041-8{_}2675{_}The arrangement irritated her unreasonably.
10041-8{_}2676{_}She wanted to disarrange these dog-eared pamphlets, to throw them on the floor, to destroy them.
10041-8{_}2677{_}She wondered how many other miserable people had tried to read these hateful books while they waited in this abominable room.
10041-8{_}2678{_}She started when the door of the consultation-room opened.
10041-8{_}2679{_}The doctor was patting the silk glove of a harassed-looking woman in black as he escorted her to the outer door, and was assuring her that everything was going very well indeed, and that she was not to worry, and so on.
10041-8{_}2680{_}And presently he spoke with Patricia, for a long while, quite levelly, of matters which it is not suitable to record.
10041-8{_}2681{_}Discreet man that he was, Wendell Pemberton could not entirely conceal his wonder that Patricia should have remained so long in ignorance of her condition.
10041-8{_}2682{_}He spoke concerning malformation and functional weaknesses and, although obscurely because of the bugbear of professional courtesy, voiced his opinion that Patricia had not received the most adroit medical treatment at the time of little Roger's birth.
10041-8{_}2683{_}She was dividedly conscious of a desire to laugh and of the notion that she must remain outwardly serious, because though this horrible Pemberton man was talking abject nonsense, she would presently be having him as a dinner-guest.
10041-8{_}2684{_}But what if he were not talking nonsense?
10041-8{_}2685{_}The possibility, considered, roused a sensation of falling through infinity.
10041-8{_}2686{_}"Yes, yes," Patricia civilly assented.
10041-8{_}2687{_}"These young doctors have taken this out of me, and that out of me, as you might take the works out of a watch.
10041-8{_}2688{_}And it has done no good; and they were mistaken in their first diagnoses, because what they took for true osteomalacia was only---- Would you mind telling me again?
10041-8{_}2689{_}Oh, yes; I had only a pseudo-osteomalacic rhachitic pelvis, to begin with.
10041-8{_}2690{_}To think of anybody's being mistaken about a simple little trouble like that!
10041-8{_}2691{_}And I suppose I was just born with it, like my mother and all those other luckless women with Musgrave blood in them?"
10041-8{_}2692{_}"Fehling and Schliephake at least consider this variety of pelvic anomaly to be congenital in the majority of cases.
10041-8{_}2693{_}But, without going into the question of heredity at all, I think it only, fair to tell you, Mrs. Musgrave----" And Pemberton went on talking.
10041-8{_}2694{_}Neither of the two showed any emotion.
10041-8{_}2695{_}The doctor went on talking.
10041-8{_}2696{_}Patricia did not listen.
10041-8{_}2697{_}The man was talking, she comprehended, but to her his words seemed blurred and indistinguishable.
10041-8{_}2698{_}"Like a talking-machine when it isn't wound up enough," she decided.
10041-8{_}2699{_}Subconsciously Patricia was thinking, "You have two big beads of perspiration on your nose, and if I were to allude to the fact you would very probably die of embarrassment."
10041-8{_}2700{_}Aloud Patricia said: "You mean, then, that, to cap it all, a functional disorder of my heart has become organic, so that I would inevitably die under another operation?
10041-8{_}2701{_}or even at a sudden shock?
10041-8{_}2702{_}And that particular operation is now the solitary chance of saving my life!
10041-8{_}2703{_}The dilemma is neat, isn't it?
10041-8{_}2704{_}How God must laugh at the jokes He contrives," said Patricia.
10041-8{_}2705{_}"I wish that I could laugh.
10041-8{_}2706{_}And I will.
10041-8{_}2707{_}I don't care whether you think me a reprobate or not, Dr. Pemberton, I want a good stiff drink of whiskey--the Musgrave size."
10041-8{_}2708{_}He gave it to her.
10041-8{_}2709{_}II   Patricia had as yet an hour to spend in Lichfield before her train left.
10041-8{_}2710{_}She passed it in the garden of her own home, where she had first seen Rudolph Musgrave and he had fought with Pevensey.
10041-8{_}2711{_}All that seemed very long ago.
10041-8{_}2712{_}The dahlia leaves, she noticed, were edged with yellow.
10041-8{_}2713{_}She must look to it that the place was more frequently watered; and that the bulbs were dug up in September.
10041-8{_}2714{_}Next year she meant to set the dahlias thinly, like a hedge....  "Oh, yes, I meant to.
10041-8{_}2715{_}Only I won't be alive next year," she recollected.
10041-8{_}2716{_}She went about the garden to see if Ned had weeded out the wild-pea vines--a pest which had invaded the trim place lately.
10041-8{_}2717{_}Only a few of the intruders remained, burnt-out and withered as they are annually by the mid-summer sun.
10041-8{_}2718{_}There would be no more fight until next April.
10041-8{_}2719{_}"Oh, and I have prayed to You, I have always tried to do what You wanted, and I never asked You to let me be born locked up in a good-for-nothing Musgrave body!
10041-8{_}2720{_}And You won't even let me see a wild-pea vine again!
10041-8{_}2721{_}That isn't much to ask, I think.
10041-8{_}2722{_}But You won't let me do it.
10041-8{_}2723{_}You really do have rather funny notions about Your jokes."
10041-8{_}2724{_}She began to laugh.
10041-8{_}2725{_}"Oh, very well!"
10041-8{_}2726{_}Patricia said aloud.
10041-8{_}2727{_}"It is none of my affair that You elect to run Your world on an extremely humorous basis."
10041-8{_}2728{_}She was at Matocton in good time for luncheon.
10041-8{_}2729{_}III   Colonel Musgrave had a brief interview with his wife after luncheon.
10041-8{_}2730{_}He began with quiet remonstrance, and ended with an unheard extenuation of his presumption.
10041-8{_}2731{_}Patricia's speech on this occasion was of an unfettered and heady nature.
10041-8{_}2732{_}"You ought to be ashamed of yourself," she said, when she had finally paused for breath, and had wiped away her tears, and had powdered her nose, viciously, "to bully a weak and defenseless woman in this way.
10041-8{_}2733{_}I dare say everybody in the house has heard us--brawling and squabbling just like a hod-carrier and his wife.
10041-8{_}2734{_}What's that?
10041-8{_}2735{_}You haven't said a word for fifteen minutes?
10041-8{_}2736{_}Oh, la, la, la!
10041-8{_}2737{_}well, I don't care.
10041-8{_}2738{_}Anyhow, I have, and I am perfectly sure they heard me, and I am sure I don't care in the least, and it's all your fault, anyway.
10041-8{_}2739{_}Oh, but you have an abominable nature, Rudolph--a mean and cruel and suspicious nature.
10041-8{_}2740{_}Your bald-headed little Charteris is nothing whatever to me; and I would have been quite willing to give him up if you had spoken to me in a decent manner about it.
10041-8{_}2741{_}You only _said_----?
10041-8{_}2742{_}I don't care what you said; and besides, if you did speak to me in a decent manner, it simply shows that your thoughts were so horrid and vulgar that even you weren't so abandoned as to dare to put them into words.
10041-8{_}2743{_}Very well, then, I won't be seen so much with him in future.
10041-8{_}2744{_}I realize you are quite capable of beating me if I don't give way to your absurd prejudices.
10041-8{_}2745{_}Yes, you are, Rudolph; you're just the sort of man to take pleasure in beating a woman.
10041-8{_}2746{_}After the exhibition of temper you've given this afternoon, I believe you are capable of anything.
10041-8{_}2747{_}Hand me that parasol!
10041-8{_}2748{_}Don't keep on talking to me; for I don't wish to hear anything you have to say.
10041-8{_}2749{_}You're simply driving me to my grave with your continual nagging and abuse and fault-finding.
10041-8{_}2750{_}I'm sure I wish I were dead as much as you do.
10041-8{_}2751{_}Is my hat on straight?
10041-8{_}2752{_}How do you expect me to see into that mirror if you stand directly in front of it?
10041-8{_}2753{_}There!
10041-8{_}2754{_}not content with robbing me of every pleasure in life, I verily believe you were going to let me go downstairs with my hat cocked over one ear.
10041-8{_}2755{_}And don't you snort and look at me like that.
10041-8{_}2756{_}I'm not going to meet Mr. Charteris.
10041-8{_}2757{_}I'm going driving with Felix Kennaston; he asked me at luncheon.
10041-8{_}2758{_}I suppose you'll object to him next; you object to all my friends.
10041-8{_}2759{_}Very well!
10041-8{_}2760{_}Now you've made me utterly miserable for the entire afternoon, and I'm sure I hope you are satisfied."
10041-8{_}2761{_}There was a rustle of skirts, and the door slammed.
10041-8{_}2762{_}IV   Colonel Musgrave went to his own room, where he spent an interval in meditation.
10041-8{_}2763{_}He opened his desk and took out a small packet of papers, some of which he read listlessly.
10041-8{_}2764{_}How curiously life re-echoed itself!
10041-8{_}2765{_}he reflected, for here, again, were castby love-letters potent to breed mischief; and his talk with Polly Ashmeade had been peculiarly reminiscent of his more ancient talk with Clarice Pendomer.
10041-8{_}2766{_}Everything that happened seemed to have happened before.
10041-8{_}2767{_}But presently he shook his head, sighing.
10041-8{_}2768{_}Chance had put into his hands a weapon, and a formidable weapon, it seemed to him, but the colonel did not care to use it.
10041-8{_}2769{_}He preferred to strike with some less grimy cudgel.
10041-8{_}2770{_}Then he rang for one of the servants, questioned him, and was informed that Mr. Charteris had gone down to the beach just after luncheon.
10041-8{_}2771{_}A moment later, Colonel Musgrave was walking through the gardens in this direction.
10041-8{_}2772{_}As he came to the thicket which screens the beach, he called Charteris's name loudly, in order to ascertain his whereabouts.
10041-8{_}2773{_}And the novelist's voice answered--yet not at once, but after a brief silence.
10041-8{_}2774{_}It chanced that, at this moment, Musgrave had come to a thin place in the thicket, and could plainly see Mr. Charteris; he was concealing some white object in the hollow of a log that lay by the river.
10041-8{_}2775{_}A little later, Musgrave came out upon the beach, and found Charteris seated upon the same log, an open book upon his knees, and looking back over his shoulder wonderingly.
10041-8{_}2776{_}"Oh," said John Charteris, "so it was you, Rudolph?
10041-8{_}2777{_}I could not imagine who it was that called."
10041-8{_}2778{_}"Yes--I wanted a word with you, Jack."
10041-8{_}2779{_}Now, there are five little red-and-white bath-houses upon the beach at Matocton; the nearest of them was some thirty feet from Mr. Charteris.
10041-8{_}2780{_}It might have been either imagination or the prevalent breeze, but Musgrave certainly thought he heard a door closing.
10041-8{_}2781{_}Moreover, as he walked around the end of the log, he glanced downward as in a casual manner, and perceived a protrusion which bore an undeniable resemblance to the handle of a parasol.
10041-8{_}2782{_}Musgrave whistled, though, at the bottom of his heart, he was not surprised; and then, he sat down upon the log, and for a moment was silent.
10041-8{_}2783{_}"A beautiful evening," said Mr. Charteris.
10041-8{_}2784{_}Musgrave lighted a cigarette.
10041-8{_}2785{_}"Jack, I have something rather difficult to say to you--yes, it is deuced difficult, and the sooner it is over the better.
10041-8{_}2786{_}I--why, confound it all, man!
10041-8{_}2787{_}I want you to stop making love to my wife."
10041-8{_}2788{_}Mr. Charteris's eyebrows rose.
10041-8{_}2789{_}"Really, Colonel Musgrave----."

10041-8{_}3048{_}You needn't bother to come."
10041-8{_}3049{_}Then Mr. Charteris laughed--a choking, sobbing laugh.
10041-8{_}3050{_}He raised his hands impotently toward heaven.
10041-8{_}3051{_}"And to think," he cried, "to think that a man may love a woman with his whole heart--with all that is best and noblest in him--and she understand him so little!"
10041-8{_}3052{_}"I do not think I have misunderstood you," Patricia said, in a crisp voice.
10041-8{_}3053{_}"Your proposition was very explicit.
10041-8{_}3054{_}I--am sorry.
10041-8{_}3055{_}I thought I had found one thing in the world which I would regret to leave--"  "And you really believed that I could sully the great love I bear you by stooping to--that!
10041-8{_}3056{_}You really believed that I would sacrifice to you my home life, my honor, my prospects--all that a man can give--without testing the quality of your love!
10041-8{_}3057{_}You did not know that I spoke to try you--you actually did not know!
10041-8{_}3058{_}Eh, but yours is a light nature, Patricia!
10041-8{_}3059{_}I do not reproach you, for you are only as your narrow Philistine life has made you.
10041-8{_}3060{_}Yet I had hoped better things of you, Patricia.
10041-8{_}3061{_}But you, who pretend to care for me, have leaped at your first opportunity to pain me--and, if it be any comfort to you, I confess you have pained me beyond words."
10041-8{_}3062{_}And he sank down on the log, and buried his face in his hands.
10041-8{_}3063{_}She came to him--it was pitiable to see how she came to him, laughing and sobbing all in one breath--and knelt humbly by his side, and raised a grieved, shamed, penitent face to his.
10041-8{_}3064{_}"Forgive me!"
10041-8{_}3065{_}she wailed; "oh, forgive me!"
10041-8{_}3066{_}"You have pained me beyond words, Patricia," he repeated.
10041-8{_}3067{_}He was not angry--only sorrowful and very much hurt.
10041-8{_}3068{_}"Ah, Jack!
10041-8{_}3069{_}dear Jack, forgive me!"
10041-8{_}3070{_}Mr. Charteris sighed.
10041-8{_}3071{_}"But, of course, I forgive you, Patricia," he said.
10041-8{_}3072{_}"I cannot help it, though, that I am foolishly sensitive where you are concerned.
10041-8{_}3073{_}And I had hoped you knew as much."
10041-8{_}3074{_}She was happy now.
10041-8{_}3075{_}"Dear boy," she murmured, "don't you see it's just these constant proofs of the greatness and the wonderfulness of your love--Really, though, Jack, wasn't it too horrid of me to misunderstand you so?
10041-8{_}3076{_}Are you quite sure you're forgiven me entirely--without any nasty little reservations?"
10041-8{_}3077{_}Mr. Charteris was quite sure.
10041-8{_}3078{_}His face was still sad, but it was benevolent.
10041-8{_}3079{_}"Don't you see," she went on, "that it's just these things that make me care for you so much, and feel sure as eggs is eggs we will be happy?
10041-8{_}3080{_}Ah, Jack, we will be so utterly happy that I am almost afraid to think of it!"
10041-8{_}3081{_}Patricia wiped away the last tear, and laughed, and added, in a matter-of-fact fashion: "There's a train at six-five in the morning; we can leave by that, before anyone is up."
10041-8{_}3082{_}Charteris started.
10041-8{_}3083{_}"Your husband loves you," he said, in gentle reproof.
10041-8{_}3084{_}"And quite candidly, you know, Rudolph is worth ten of me."
10041-8{_}3085{_}"Bah, I tell you, that was a comedy for my benefit," she protested, and began to laugh.
10041-8{_}3086{_}Patricia was unutterably happy now, because she, and not John Charteris, had been in the wrong.
10041-8{_}3087{_}"Poor Rudolph!--he has such a smug horror of the divorce-court that he would even go so far as to pretend to be in love with his own wife in order to keep out of it.
10041-8{_}3088{_}Really, Jack, both our better-halves are horribly commonplace and they will be much better off without us."
10041-8{_}3089{_}"You forget that Rudolph has my word of honor," said Mr. Charteris, in indignation.
10041-8{_}3090{_}And that instant, with one of his baffling changes of mood, he began to laugh.
10041-8{_}3091{_}"Really, though, Patricia, you are very pretty.
10041-8{_}3092{_}You are April embodied in sweet flesh; your soul is just a wisp of April cloud, and your life an April day, half sun that only seems to warm, and half tempest that only plays at ferocity; but you are very pretty.
10041-8{_}3093{_}That is why I am thinking, light-headedly, it would be a fine and past doubt an agreeable exploit to give up everything for such a woman, and am complacently comparing myself to Antony at Actium.
10041-8{_}3094{_}I am thinking it would be an interesting episode in one's _Life and Letters_.
10041-8{_}3095{_}You see, my dear, I honestly believe the world revolves around John Charteris--although of course I would never admit that to you if I thought for a moment you would take me seriously."
10041-8{_}3096{_}Then presently, sighing, he was grave again.
10041-8{_}3097{_}"But, no!
10041-8{_}3098{_}Rudolph has my word of honor," Mr. Charteris repeated, and with unconcealed regret.
10041-8{_}3099{_}"Ah, does that matter?"
10041-8{_}3100{_}she cried.
10041-8{_}3101{_}"Does anything matter, except that we love each other?
10041-8{_}3102{_}I tell you I have given the best part of my life to that man, but I mean to make the most of what is left.
10041-8{_}3103{_}He has had my youth, my love--there was a time, you know, when I actually fancied I cared for him--and he has only made me unhappy.
10041-8{_}3104{_}I hate him, I loathe him, I detest him, I despise him!
10041-8{_}3105{_}I never intend to speak to him again--oh, yes, I shall have to at supper, I suppose, but that doesn't count.
10041-8{_}3106{_}And I tell you I mean to be happy in the only way that's possible.
10041-8{_}3107{_}Everyone has a right to do that.
10041-8{_}3108{_}A woman has an especial right to take her share of happiness in any way she can, because her hour of it is so short.
10041-8{_}3109{_}Sometimes--sometimes the woman knows how short it is and it almost frightens her....
10041-8{_}3110{_}But at best, a woman can be really happy through love alone, Jack dear, and it's only when we are young and good to look at that men care for us; after that, there is nothing left but to take to either religion or hand-embroidery, so what does it matter, after all?
10041-8{_}3111{_}Yes, they all grow tired after a while.
10041-8{_}3112{_}Jack, I am only a vain and frivolous person of superlative charm, but I love you very much, my dear, and I solemnly swear to commit suicide the moment my first wrinkle arrives.
10041-8{_}3113{_}You shall never grow tired of me, my dear."
10041-8{_}3114{_}She laughed to think how true this was.
10041-8{_}3115{_}She hurried on: "Jack, kneel down at once, and swear that you are perfectly sore with loving me, as that ridiculous person says in Dickens, and whose name I never could remember.
10041-8{_}3116{_}Oh, I forgot--Dickens caricatures nature, doesn't he, and isn't read by really cultured people?
10041-8{_}3117{_}You will have to educate me up to your level, Jack, and I warn you in advance you will not have time to do it.
10041-8{_}3118{_}Yes, I am quite aware that I am talking nonsense, and am on the verge of hysterics, thank you, but I rather like it.
10041-8{_}3119{_}It is because I am going to have you all to myself for whatever future there is, and the thought makes me quite drunk.
10041-8{_}3120{_}Will you kindly ring for the patrol-wagon, Jack?
10041-8{_}3121{_}Jack, are you quite sure you love me?
10041-8{_}3122{_}Are you perfectly certain you never loved any one else half so much?
10041-8{_}3123{_}No, don't answer me, for I intend to do all the talking for both of us for the future!
10041-8{_}3124{_}I shall tyrannize over you frightfully, and you will like it.
10041-8{_}3125{_}All I ask in return is that you will be a good boy--by which I mean a naughty boy--and do solemnly swear, promise and affirm that you will meet me at the side-door at half-past five in the morning, with a portmanteau and the intention of never going back to your wife.
10041-8{_}3126{_}You swear it?
10041-8{_}3127{_}Thank you so much!
10041-8{_}3128{_}Now, I think I would like to cry for a few minutes, and, after that, we will go back to the house, before supper is over and my eyes are perfectly crimson."
10041-8{_}3129{_}In fact, Mr. Charteris had consented.
10041-8{_}3130{_}Patricia was irresistible as she pleaded and mocked and scolded and coaxed and laughed and cried, all in one bewildering breath.
10041-8{_}3131{_}Her plan was simple; it was to slip out of Matocton at dawn, and walk to the near-by station.
10041-8{_}3132{_}There they would take the train, and snap their fingers at convention.
10041-8{_}3133{_}The scheme sounded preposterous in outline, but she demonstrated its practicability in performance.
10041-8{_}3134{_}And Mr. Charteris consented.
10041-8{_}3135{_}Rudolph Musgrave sat in the shadow of the cedar with fierce and confused emotions whirling in his soul.
10041-8{_}3136{_}He certainly had never thought of this contingency.
10041-8{_}3137{_}PART EIGHT - HARVEST    "Time was I coveted the woes they rued   Whose love commemorates them,--I that meant   To get like grace of love then!--and intent   To win as they had done love's plenitude,   Rapture and havoc, vauntingly I sued   That love like theirs might make a toy of me,   At will caressed, at will (if publicly)   Demolished, as Love found or found not good.
10041-8{_}3138{_}"To-day I am no longer overbrave.
10041-8{_}3139{_}I have a fever,--I that always knew   This hour was certain!--and am too weak to rave,   Too tired to seek (as later I must do)   Tried remedies--time, manhood and the grave--   To drug, abate and banish love of you."
10041-8{_}3140{_}ALLEN ROSSITER.
10041-8{_}3141{_}_A Fragment_.
10041-8{_}3142{_}I   When Patricia and Charteris had left the beach, Colonel Musgrave parted the underbrush and stepped down upon the sand He must have air--air and an open place wherein to fight this out.
10041-8{_}3143{_}Night had risen about him in bland emptiness.
10041-8{_}3144{_}There were no stars overhead, but a patient, wearied, ancient moon pushed through the clouds.
10041-8{_}3145{_}The trees and the river conferred with one another doubtfully.
10041-8{_}3146{_}He paced up and down the beach....  Musgrave laughed in the darkness.
10041-8{_}3147{_}His heart was racing, racing in him, and his thoughts were blown foam.
10041-8{_}3148{_}He raised his hat and bowed fantastically in the darkness, because the colonel loved his gesture.
10041-8{_}3149{_}"Signor Lucifer, I present my compliments.
10041-8{_}3150{_}You have discoursed with me very plausibly.
10041-8{_}3151{_}I honor your cunning, signor, but if you are indeed a gentleman, as I have always heard, you will now withdraw and permit me to regard the matter from a standpoint other than my own.
10041-8{_}3152{_}For the others are weak, signor; as you have doubtless discovered, good women and bad men are the weakest of their sex.
10041-8{_}3153{_}I am the strongest among them, for all that I am no Hercules; and the outcome of this matter must rest with me."
10041-8{_}3154{_}So he sat presently upon the log, where Charteris had sat when Musgrave came to this beach at sunset.
10041-8{_}3155{_}Very long ago that seemed now.
10041-8{_}3156{_}For now the colonel was tired--physically outworn, it seemed to him, as if after prolonged exertion--and now the moon looked down upon him, passionless, cold, inexorable, and seemed to await the colonel's decision.
10041-8{_}3157{_}And it was woefully hard to come to any decision.
